You have to know your own game. If you do play better with a lead, with less tension and pressure, go ahead and press the issue. If you make mistakes with that approach, stay with what got you the lead in the first place. Just concentrate on doing it better. As the saying goes, “Dance with who brung ya.”

>你必须了解自己的比赛方式。如果你在领先时确实打得更好，压力和紧张感也更小，那就放手一搏，主动施压。如果这种打法出现失误，那就回到最初让你取得领先的方法上。只需专注于把事情做得更好。正如那句俗话所说：“跟带来你的人跳舞。”

In either case a primary factor is mental alertness and an understanding of the dynamics of the situation. You’ve got the lead with that break. Avoid becoming careless. Don’t make stupid mistakes. Don’t give up your advantage by getting mentally lazy.

>无论是哪种情况，首要因素都是保持心理警觉，并理解当前局势的动态。你已经取得了破发的优势，不要变得粗心大意。不要犯愚蠢的错误。不要因为心理上变得懒惰而失去优势。

MY MOTTO: D.R.M.

>我的座右铭：D.R.M。

As I mentioned, my motto is D.R.M; “Don’t Rush Me.” Tennis players tend to speed up when they go ahead (or fall behind). It hurts their [[null|]]game. You feel good when you grab a break to go ahead. You’re pumped. It’s natural to step up the pace. But be careful. That’s when mistakes happen. A double fault. An ill-advised attempt at a forehand winner. An approach shot at the wrong time. Bing. Bing. Bing. You’ve lost the break. So be deliberate. Don’t race to the line and jump into the next point. Think a little about what you’re going to do next. Don’t slow it down. Just don’t speed it up.

>正如我之前提到的，我的座右铭是“D.R.M”——“别急我（Don’t Rush Me）”。网球选手往往在领先（或落后）时会加快节奏。这会损害他们的比赛。当你拿到破发优势时，你会感觉很好，情绪高涨，加快节奏是自然的。但要小心，这正是失误发生的时刻。双误、仓促的正手制胜球尝试、在错误时机打出的上网击球……“叮——”“叮——”“叮——”，你已经失去了这个破发点。因此，你要有条不紊，不要急着进入下一拍，稍微想一想接下来该怎么做。不要放慢节奏，只是不要加快节奏。

Here’s my antirushing device. I’ll pick out a spot on the back wall (in front of the spectator seats) or a mark on the court five or ten feet behind the baseline. Between each point I will actually go to that mark and touch it with my racket or hand, or at least look at it. I walk back to it, touch it, and then go back to the baseline. It prevents me from jumping into points carelessly. When I’ve got a lead I want to avoid getting careless.

>我的“防急躁装置”就是这样的：我会在后墙（ spectator seats 前方）选一个点，或者在底线后五到十英尺处选一个标记。每一分之间，我会真正走到那个点，用球拍或手去触碰它，或者至少看一下。我走回去触碰它，然后再回到底线。这能防止我仓促地进入下一拍。当我领先时，我尤其要避免轻敌。

THE BEST AT STRETCHING A LEAD

>最擅长扩大优势的高手 

>[!note]- 译者注：
此标题意指那些最擅长在比赛中扩大领先优势的选手，译为“最擅长扩大优势的高手”既保留原意，又符合中文表达习惯。

Jimmy Connors, John McEnroe, and Ivan Lendl are the absolute masters on tour when it comes to holding and stretching a lead. Nobody else in tennis even comes close, although Jim Courier is showing signs of wanting to join the club. When I’m down a break at 2–4 against Lendl the next time I look up at the scoreboard it’ll say 6–2, 3–0 Lendl. Before you even know it’s happening he’s turned the match into a rout. Connors and Mac do the same.

>吉米·康纳斯、约翰·麦肯罗和伊万·伦德尔是巡回赛中在保持和扩大领先优势方面绝对的高手。其他球员根本无法望其项背，尽管吉姆·库尔特似乎正试图加入这个俱乐部。当我以2-4落后对战伦德尔时，下一次我抬头看比分牌，上面已经显示6-2，3-0伦德尔。你还没意识到发生了什么，他便已将比赛变成了一场屠杀。康纳斯和麦肯罗也是一样。

Most players don’t feed on a lead like they do. There’s something inside them that gets absolutely bloodthirsty when they go ahead. It’s one of the reasons they’re such great champions. When they’ve got you down and their foot is on the back of your neck they’re not satisfied. They want to get both feet on the back of your neck. And when they’ve got both feet on the back of your neck they want to start jumping up and down on it. They are unique. And very dangerous.

>大多数球员在领先时并不会像他们那样疯狂地汲取优势。他们内心深处有一种东西，一旦领先就会变得极度饥渴。这也是他们成为伟大冠军的原因之一。当他们把你逼到绝境，脚踩在你脖子上时，他们并不满足。他们想要把双脚都踩在你脖子上。而当双脚都踩上去后，他们还想跳起来踩个够。他们是独特的，而且非常危险。

>[!note]- 该段文字通过生动的比喻，形象地描绘了顶尖选手在领先时的侵略性和不满足感，翻译时保留了这种强烈的画面感和情绪张力。

Connors and McEnroe instinctively pound on the opponent even harder when they get ahead. I believe they avoid getting casual with a lead because they enjoy the thrill of beating on an opponent more than the feeling of being comfortable. They go for the throat when they have [[null|]]the chance. When they get up a break they never think about just holding serve to win the set. They want to get another break. And another break.

>康纳斯和麦肯罗在领先时会本能地加大对对手的施压。我认为他们之所以不轻视领先优势，是因为他们更享受击败对手的刺激感，而非仅仅感到舒适。他们一旦有机会，就会直取要害。当他们取得破发优势时，从不会仅仅想着保住发球局以赢得这一盘，他们渴望再破一次发球局。再破一次。

They don’t want you to get another point. Lendl, too. They get into a feeding frenzy with a lead. It’s almost scary how focused and intense they can get. Courier now shows it in his game. Watch him play when he’s ahead. He hits harder and goes for more at critical times than almost anybody else out there.

>他们不想让你再得一分，伦德尔也一样。一旦领先，他们就会陷入疯狂的进攻状态。他们专注和投入的程度几乎令人感到害怕。库尔库奇现在在比赛中已经体现了这一点。看看他在领先时的表现，关键时刻他击球更用力，更敢于冒险，几乎无人能及。

>[!note]- 译注：此处“feeding frenzy”意为“疯狂进攻”，根据中文表达习惯进行意译。

BE A GOOD LIAR

>做一名好骗子 

>[!note]- 译者注：
此标题为本书中一节标题，原意为“学会在比赛中保持冷静与自信”，此处采用直译，保留其“欺骗”与“伪装”的双关意味，以符合原文风格。

Very few players are like those guys. And just like most others, I tend to get comfortable when I’m ahead. The reason is simple and straightforward. Pressure makes us feel uncomfortable. We don’t like it. So our mind will seize on any positive development as a reason to worry less, to feel less pressure and subsequently think and play with reduced intensity. So when I do get up a break I try to provide myself with a mental attitude that keeps me in a “hungry” mode. Here’s what I do: I lie to myself.

>很少有球员会像那些人一样。和大多数人一样，当我领先时，我往往会变得放松。原因很简单也很直接。压力会让我们感到不舒服，我们不喜欢这种感觉。因此，我们的大脑会抓住任何积极的变化，把它当作减轻担忧、减少压力的理由，从而让我们的思维和表现变得不再那么专注和激烈。所以，当我成功取得破发时，我会努力让自己保持一种“饥饿”的心态。具体我怎么做呢？我对自己撒谎。

I’ll think, “Brad, pick it up now. You’re down a break (even though I’m not). Don’t fall behind. Work harder. You’ve got to break him back. This isn’t going to be easy.” It works. I feel like I’m fighting to catch up instead of sitting on and relaxing with a lead.

>我会想：“布拉德，现在赶紧追分吧。你已经落后一分了（尽管我并没有落后）。别掉队，加把劲。你必须再次破发。这可不容易。” 这种方法很奏效。我感觉像是在努力追赶，而不是坐享优势、轻松应对。

In fact, the bigger the lead, the more I want to be concerned. I keep telling myself that unless I work even harder I’ll lose. The bigger the lead the more consciously I work at being mentally engaged. When I’m behind it happens automatically, the emergency alarm goes off by itself. When I’m ahead I have to work on myself to keep my nose in the fight. I believe most recreational players are exactly the same way.

>事实上，领先越多，我反而越担心。我不断告诉自己，除非我更加努力，否则我就会输。领先越多，我越有意识地让自己保持专注和投入。当我落后时，这种状态会自动出现，就像警报器自己响起来一样。而当我领先时，我却必须主动提醒自己，不能松懈，要一直保持战斗状态。我相信大多数业余选手都是这样。

>[!note]- 说明：这里的“keep my nose in the fight”意为“保持战斗状态”，用“保持战斗状态”表达更符合中文习惯。

What Connors, McEnroe, Lendl, and increasingly Courier do is very difficult to accomplish, and I don’t recommend it. They increase the risk level of shots they take. They go into attack mode with a confidence that’s really amazing. You’ve heard the phrase, “protecting a lead”? Not these guys. They’re out to stretch their lead. And they do it because somehow when they get ahead they aren’t afraid to start taking risks. And they can do it without making many mistakes.

>康纳斯、麦肯罗、伦德尔，还有越来越多的库尔库奇，他们所做的事情非常难，我也不建议普通人去效仿。他们敢于打出高风险的球。他们带着一种令人难以置信的信心进入进攻状态。你听过“保住领先优势”这句话吗？这些人可不会这么想。他们想要扩大自己的领先优势。他们之所以能做到这一点，是因为在领先的时候，他们竟然不害怕冒险。而且他们还能做到少犯错误。

My approach is different and I believe better for the average club [[null|]]player’s game. Most players make mistakes when they start getting aggressive and hitting harder. My goal is to continue doing exactly what I did to get ahead, only better. I don’t work on increasing my power. I work on increasing my awareness and concentration. I don’t want to change my game (after all, it got me ahead). I want to work on my mind so that I stay on track. You should do the same.

>我的方法有所不同，我认为对普通俱乐部球员的打法更为有效。大多数球员在开始变得激进、大力击球时反而会犯错。我的目标是继续做那些让我取得领先优势的事情，只不过做得更好。我不追求增加力量，而是专注于提高意识和专注力。我不想改变我的打法（毕竟，正是这种打法让我取得领先）。我想通过锻炼我的心理，让自己始终专注于目标。你们也应该这样做。

Players at all levels start feeling a great urge to experiment with new tactics and shots when they get ahead. It’s strange thinking. They get a lead doing one thing and then want to hold or increase that lead by doing something else, usually something they’re not as good at or they’d have done it originally! When you’re ahead, keep doing exactly what worked to get you ahead.

>在任何级别，当球员取得领先时，他们都会产生一种强烈的尝试新战术和新击球方式的冲动。这是一种奇怪的思维方式。他们原本通过做某件事取得领先，但随后却想通过做其他事情来维持或扩大这个优势，而这些事情通常不是他们擅长的，或者他们原本就不打算这么做！当你处于领先时，继续做那些让你取得领先的有效动作。

I go even further than that. I don’t change anything when I’m leading. I usually keep the same shirt (even if it’s soaked), the same racket, the same towel to wipe off sweat, and I want to keep the same ball in play after I win a point. Change nothing.

>我甚至走得更远。我在领先时也不会改变任何东西。我通常会一直穿着同一件球衣（即使它已经湿透了），用同样的球拍，同样的毛巾擦汗，而且我希望在赢下一分之后，继续用同一只球。一切都不变。

## 9 5\. Stopping the Match From Slipping Away

>9 5\. 防止比赛失控

When I feel that a match is slipping away from me (or in danger of slipping away) I want to make changes, strategically, mentally, and physically. In order to do that I have to be observant. I have to ask, “Who’s doing what to whom?” If I can answer that correctly I’ll know where the adjustments in my game plan need to be made.

>当我感觉到一场比赛正在从我手中溜走（或有溜走的危险）时，我想要从战略、心理和身体层面做出改变。要做到这一点，我必须保持警觉，必须问自己：“是谁在对谁做些什么？”如果我能够正确回答这个问题，就能清楚地知道我的战术安排需要在哪方面做出调整。

First I ask myself:

>首先，我会问自己：

1\. Am I following my game plan?

>1\. 我是否在按照自己的战术计划进行比赛？

Then, if I am following my plan I ask:

>接着，如果我按照我的计划进行，我会问：

2\. What is my opponent doing to defeat my strategy?

>2\. 我的对手在用什么方法来击败我的战术？

Obviously, if for some reason the answer to the first question is no, I’ll want to get back to what I said I would do in my pre-match preparation. I’ll want to at least try and give my game plan a chance to work. Most recreational players tend to give up on their strategy too soon. They lose a few points or games with it and abandon ship. Give it a chance to work! Stay with it long enough to test your opponent.

>显然，如果由于某种原因，对第一个问题的答案是否定的，我就会想回到我赛前准备时所说的计划。我想至少尝试让我的战术有机会发挥作用。大多数休闲球员往往过早地放弃自己的策略。他们用它输掉几分或几局后，就放弃了。给它一个机会吧！坚持足够长的时间，去试探你的对手。

However, if you continue to struggle you will need to address [[null|]]slippage. When a player breaks you and consolidates the break (holds serve) you have to be very sure it doesn’t get any worse. I always figure I can come back from a break down; two breaks down is serious trouble.

>然而，如果你继续挣扎，就必须面对[[null|]]失分（slippage）。当一名球员破发后并成功保发（即保住发球局）时，你必须非常确定情况不会进一步恶化。我总是认为自己可以从被破发后反败为胜，但如果被破发两次，那就真的陷入困境了。

It’s at that point in the match when D.R.M. (Don’t Rush Me) is again very important. I know that mistakes tend to come in bunches. Suddenly, I’m not a little bit behind—I’m a lot behind. It’s like stepping on a banana peel. Just like that you can fall on your butt. And it’s right at that point that I want to control the tempo of the match. I want to be deliberate. I want to avoid rushing. I don’t want my opponent to cruise on that momentum they’ve built.

>比赛到了那个关键时刻，再次体现出“别急（D.R.M.）”的重要性。我知道失误往往会接连出现。突然之间，我不只是稍微落后，而是大大落后了。就像踩到了香蕉皮，一下子就能摔个狗啃泥。正是在这样的时候，我想要掌控比赛的节奏。我想有意识地、有条不紊地进行。我不想仓促行事。我不希望对手乘着他们已建立的势头一路顺风。

That’s when I’ll make sure to walk back and touch the mark on the court or back fence between points. During that time I’ll be giving myself a pep talk, “C’mon Brad. Let’s go! Work a little bit.” Or I’ll towel off. (You’ll often see a player take a towel from one ballperson and after using it walk to the other side of the court and hand it to another ballperson. It’s just a mechanical device to slow things down and stop the slide from turning into an avalanche.)

>那就是我确保走回去触摸场地边线或后网标记的时候了。在那段时间里，我会给自己打打气：“布拉德，加油！我们再来一次！稍微努力一点。”或者我会用毛巾擦擦汗。（你经常会看到一名球员从一名球童那里接过毛巾，用完后走到场地另一边，再递给另一个球童。这只是一个机械性的手段，用来放慢节奏，防止情绪滑坡演变成无法控制的崩溃。）

Tying shoes, talking to the chair umpire or line officials, straightening strings, bouncing the ball before a serve—these are often just devices to cool the heat the other player has created. All done within the legal time limits (usually), but just bringing the tempo of the match back down a little. In Part III you’ll see how McEnroe, Connors, and Lendl do this with great results.

>系鞋带、跟裁判或边线裁判说话、调紧球拍弦、发球前拍打网球——这些举动往往只是用来冷却对方球员制造的紧张气氛。这些行为通常都在法定的时间范围内完成，但能略微降低比赛的节奏。在第三部分中，你将看到麦肯罗、康纳斯和伦德尔如何有效地运用这些方法，并取得了很好的效果。

When a player starts to break open a tennis match (as Lendl does so effectively) it can turn into a stampede. You can lose control of things quickly, just like a car that hits a patch of ice and is suddenly skidding out of control.

>当一名球员开始打破一场网球比赛的僵局（比如伦德尔做得非常有效）时，局势可能瞬间失控，如同一场踩踏事件。你可能迅速失去对局面的掌控，就像一辆车突然驶入结冰路面，瞬间失控滑向一边。

When that happens to me I make the tempo of the match more deliberate. Most opponents will come out of their rhythm. They’ll drop out of the zone they’re in if you interfere with their momentum. This is going on constantly among the pros.

>当我遇到这种情况时，我会放慢比赛的节奏，让整个比赛更从容。大多数对手都会因此失去原有的节奏，如果你干扰了他们的势头，他们就会从自己所处的状态中“掉线”。这在职业比赛中时时刻刻都在发生。

Pay attention during a televised match to the tempo between points. Watch what a player does when they’re behind or ahead. When they’re ahead they want to keep playing along at that same winning tempo that has given them the lead. When a good player starts falling behind watch them slow things down.

>注意观看电视转播中的比赛，留意选手在得分之间所展现的节奏。观察当球员处于领先或落后时他们的表现。当他们领先时，他们会希望保持同样的获胜节奏，以维持优势。而当一名好球员开始落后时，他们会放慢节奏。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“slow things down”既可直译为“放慢节奏”，也可理解为“调整策略”，根据上下文选择更符合中文表达习惯的译法。

[[null|]]CHANGE YOUR SHIRT

When I’m behind and looking for a change, I shake up my attitude. And I do that by going to my equipment bag, my Tools of the Trade. I may change into a dry shirt. Or put on a fresh pair of socks, have a Jolly Rancher, or just put a new sweatlet on my wrist. Just a little change to feel like it’s a new start, a fresh beginning. When I’m trying to get a break back I’ll often tie both of my shoes. I’m telling myself it’s time to bear down and work hard.

>当我落后并且想要改变状态时，我会调整自己的心态。我通过去取装备包——我的“行头”——来做到这一点。我可能会换一件干爽的衬衫，或者穿上一双新的袜子，吃一颗Jolly Rancher糖，或者只是换上一条新的腕带。这只是小小的改变，让我感觉像是一个新的开始，一个崭新的起点。当我试图扭转局势时，我经常会把两只鞋子都系好。我告诉自己，是时候全力以赴、努力拼搏了。

Remember the old right tennis shoe that helped me win $114,000 against Jim Pugh at Stratton Mountain? I actually carried it around with me for a couple of years. I thought of it as my rally shoe and would change into it when I needed a little psychological boost. I want to feel positive and confident about my chances. I want to avoid that sense of being on the run. A little equipment change helps.

>还记得那双旧的右脚网球鞋吗？它帮助我击败了吉姆·普格（Jim Pugh），赢得了114000美元，比赛地点是斯特拉顿山（Stratton Mountain）。我实际上带着它走了好几年。我把这双鞋当作我的“接球鞋”，每当需要一点心理上的提振时，我就会换上它。我想让自己对比赛的前景保持积极和自信，我想避免那种被追着跑的感觉。一点点装备的改变，就能带来帮助。

A CHANGE OF PLANS

>计划变更

At what point do you have to go further and actually change strategy? It varies from match to match and player to player. If you want a specific point in a match it’s this: when you’re down a set and a break. That’s not always the time to change, but it’s a good guideline. You may have lost the first set in a tiebreaker and then lost serve because of great shots by your opponent. This is still a close match. But if your opponent won the first set easily and is doing the same in the second, you better change. Wait much longer and you’re terminal.

>你在什么时候必须采取更进一步的行动，甚至改变策略呢？这因比赛而异，也因选手而异。如果你想具体指出比赛中的某个关键时刻，那就是：当你在决胜盘以一盘之差落后时。这不一定是立刻改变策略的最佳时机，但它是一个很好的参考点。你可能在第一盘抢七中失利，接着又在发球局中被对手的精彩击球所压制。这个时候比赛仍然非常胶着。但如果对手在第一盘轻松赢下，并且在第二盘也延续了这种优势，那你最好立刻改变策略。如果你犹豫太久，那就真的陷入绝境了。

Occasionally you will want to make a change in the first set. If you’re down 0–5 and just getting wiped out, make some adjustments to see if they work. Get them going before you start the second set.

>有时你可能会想在第一盘做出一些改变。如果你在第一盘0–5落后，而且局势已经完全失控，那就做出一些调整，看看是否奏效。在进入第二盘之前，先让这些调整发挥作用。

>[!note]- 译注：此处“get them going”意为让调整生效或让对手陷入被动，根据上下文译为“让这些调整发挥作用”更符合中文表达习惯。

If you want a specific point at which you should generally make a change, though, that’s it—down a set and a break. At that point something has to change or you will lose. The match has been underway long enough to establish a trend. And the trend shows you congratulating the winner. Change your strategy. Analyze your options and give your opponent a different look.

>如果你想找到一个具体的时间点，你应该在此时做出改变——当你落后一盘又一个发球局的时候。到了这个节点，必须有所改变，否则你将会输掉比赛。比赛已经进行得足够久，足以形成某种趋势，而这个趋势显示你正在祝贺胜利者。改变你的策略。分析你的选择，给对手一个不同的看法。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“give your opponent a different look”意为“换一种方式看待对手”，即调整战术和心态，而非字面意思。

[[null|]]If I’ve been losing by staying at the baseline I’ll try to upset my opponent by coming to the net. If my second serve is getting bossed around I’ll know it’s because my first serve isn’t going in and I’m letting my opponent see second serves. (Remember the ’87 Open against Becker? I was very conscious of keeping him from seeing many second serves.) If I’m getting passed when I go to the net I’ll either attempt to improve my approach shot or decide to stay back at the baseline. If my opponent is attacking my backhand successfully I’ll take action to reduce my vulnerability there (see The Attack to Your Backhand in chapter 7).

My coach, Tom Chivington, actually believes I play better when I’m behind than when I’ve got a lead. He may be right and if he is it’s because I’m better at handling things. I know what to do when I get behind. It’s never a panicky situation. I recognize what needs to be done and do it. Perhaps the most important thing is to do it before it’s too late. That’s how you’ll start climbing back into matches.

>我的教练汤姆·奇文顿（Tom Chivington）实际上认为，我在落后时的发挥比领先时更好。他可能是对的，如果他确实如此，那是因为我更擅长应对各种情况。我知道在落后时该做什么，这从来不是一种慌乱的局面。我清楚自己需要做什么，并且会去做。也许最重要的是，在事情变得太晚之前就采取行动。这就是你开始扭转比赛局势的方式。

## 10 6\. Tiebreaker Tactics

>10 6\. 拖延战术

During the 1993 A.T.P. tournament in San Francisco I had to play a total of three tiebreakers. I won them all, including one in the finals against Andre Agassi. My success in those tiebreakers and others was because I had a plan. Here it is.

>1993年ATP旧金山站比赛中，我一共打了三盘抢七，而且全部赢了下来，其中还包括决赛对阵安德烈·阿加西的那一盘。我在这些抢七以及其他比赛中取得成功，是因为我有一个计划。下面是这个计划。

I think of a tiebreak as a mini-set. Everything is compressed, but the components of a set are all still present. During a tiebreak you serve for the first time and receive serve for the first time. You need to break serve (a mini-break) to win. The tiebreak has a Dictate Game (or Dictate Points) at its beginning, it has the Set-up Point, and it often requires that you hold a lead or stop the tiebreak from slipping away. The dynamics are very similar to those in a regular set, but condensed and more potent.

>我认为抢七（tiebreak）就像一个小盘局（mini-set）。所有元素都被压缩了，但一盘比赛的各个组成部分依然存在。在抢七中，你第一次发球，也第一次接发球。你需要在抢七中破发（mini-break）才能赢。抢七开始时通常会有“主导球”（Dictate Game）或“主导分”（Dictate Points），接着会有“准备分”（Set-up Point），并且常常需要你保持领先，或者防止抢七被对手偷走。抢七的动态与常规盘局非常相似，只是节奏更快、强度更高。

Because the results of a tiebreaker decide who wins the set and because it’s so compressed I’m extremely aware of the tempo of the match during this period: D.R.M. is my watchword. Playing quickly and carelessly can immediately put you at a disadvantage from which you won’t recover. Three double faults in the third game of the first set may only [[null|]]cost you the game. Do the same during a tiebreak and the consequences will almost always be much more severe.

>因为抢七的结果决定了谁赢得这一盘，而且时间非常紧凑，所以我特别清楚这段时间比赛的节奏：D.R.M.（快速而谨慎）是我奉行的原则。比赛如果打得太快又太随意，会立刻让你陷入无法挽回的劣势。在第一盘的第三局出现三次双误，也许只会让你输掉这一局。但如果在抢七中也这么做，后果往往要严重得多。

I approach a tiebreak just as I do the rest of the set. You should do the same.

>我面对抢七的心态，和面对比赛其余部分的心态是一样的。你也是如此。

Approach the beginning of a tiebreak with the thought in mind that you are going to play blue-chip tennis. Let your opponent be spectacular. The first two points of a tiebreak are Dictate Points. You can seize control and put your opponent at an immediate disadvantage, in a position where they may pressure themselves into making mistakes because they’re behind. Those first two points bring increased tension to the match and so I want to be extremely careful not to go for a high-risk shot just because I’m nervous and want to end the point quickly.

>进入抢七局时，要心中想着自己将要打出“蓝筹级”的网球。让对手表现得非常出色。抢七局的前两个发球局是“主导局”（Dictate Points）。你可以借此掌控局面，让对手立刻陷入劣势，他们可能会因为落后而压力倍增，从而自己制造失误。前两个球能提升比赛的紧张感，因此我特别小心不要因为紧张而急于结束这一分，就去冒险击出高风险的球。

Separate those first two points of the tiebreak from the set you just played. Don’t just glide into them. Gather your thoughts and refocus (walk back and touch the mark on the court while you think over what your game plan is). This is not just an extension of the last game of the previous set. Make yourself isolate those first two points and play them with renewed alertness; get it in or get it back.

>把抢七中的前两个发球点，与你刚刚打完的那一盘区分开来。不要只是轻飘飘地进入这两个点，而是停下来整理思路，重新集中注意力（比如走回球场，触摸一下记号，同时回顾你的战术安排）。这不仅仅只是上一盘最后一局的延续。你要让自己把前两个发球点孤立出来，以全新的警觉性去面对它们；发得进去，或者把球打回去。

You don’t want to “play afraid,” but you don’t want to introduce loose shots or new tactics unless you’re very comfortable with them. Continue to use what was successful in getting you to the breaker.

>你不想“带着恐惧去打球”，但你也不要在没有完全适应的情况下引入新的打法或战术。继续使用那些曾帮助你来到决胜盘的策略。

The tiebreak is a separate entity and needs attention. Don’t rush. Be deliberate and know what you are going to do, especially at the beginning.

>抢七是一个独立的单元，需要特别关注。不要急于求成，要慎重对待，明确自己要做什么，尤其是在抢七开始的时候。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“抢七”指的是网球比赛中决胜局（tiebreak），在中文网球术语中通常称为“抢七”或“决胜局”，根据上下文选择更自然的表达。

Each player’s initial serve in the tiebreak is performed under high pressure. So again my goal is to get it in. I don’t like to try to do too much. I think of those first points as being similar to the start of the first set. I want to be sure early in the tiebreak to play within my game. I want to avoid being too ambitious. Often with the increased pressure of a tiebreak a player’s nervousness will cause him or her to try an inappropriate shot. I want to play steadier tennis, not flashier tennis, at this time.

>每场比赛抢七中的第一个发球，球员都处于巨大的压力之下。因此，我依然的目标是把球发出去。我不喜欢做太多复杂的尝试。我认为这些第一分和比赛第一盘的开局很相似。我希望在抢七初期就按自己的打法来打，避免过于激进。通常在抢七的压力下，球员的紧张情绪会导致他们打出不恰当的球。此时我想要打得更稳定，而不是更花哨。

Too often players will approach a tiebreak less with the thought of winning it than with the hope that their opponent will lose it for them. That’s not conservative play; it’s constricting play and it will hurt you. [[null|]]Go for your shots if they present themselves, but don’t try to jam in a winner just because you get impatient.

>太多时候，球员在进入抢七时，并不是想着如何赢下这一局，而是希望对手能替自己输掉。这并不是保守的打法，而是限制性的打法，它会伤害到你。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“constricting play”意指过于拘谨、不敢放手一搏的打法，直译为“限制性打法”虽准确，但略显生硬，故保留原意并适当调整表达。  

如果机会出现，就大胆击球，但不要因为急躁而强行强攻，试图立刻得分。

The tendency to just hope your opponent “loses it” is especially common when you get a lead during a tiebreaker. You go ahead 4–1 and suddenly get nervous, hoping the opponent will just hand it to you. This is when I will lie to myself, tell myself that I’m behind so I don’t get complacent and lose my intensity. It’s when you have to talk to yourself about what you want to do.

>当你在抢七中取得领先时，希望对手“崩溃”就是一种特别常见的心理倾向。你领先到4-1，突然就紧张起来，希望对手能“送分”给你。这时我就会对自己撒谎，告诉自己其实我处在劣势，这样就不会变得自满，也不会失去专注力。这个时候，你就必须对自己说你想要做什么。

And of course the point in a tiebreak that precedes a set point is one that I treat as very special. A Set-up Point in a tiebreak (for example, 5–3) is almost always undervalued at the club level and even sometimes at the pro level. It can move me (or my opponent) up to an opportunity to win the set or match. I want no stupid mistakes, no unnecessary risks. Squeeze your opponent like a boa constrictor. At this crucial moment in a match, where you can move up to a set point, make sure your game is under control and you’re thinking correctly.

>当然， tiebreak 中紧接 set point 的那个分，我特别重视。例如在 5–3 的 tiebreak 中，这个“set-up point”（即距离 set point 只差一分的情况）通常在俱乐部级别甚至职业级别都被低估了。这个分可能会让我（或我的对手）获得赢得这一盘甚至整场比赛的机会。我绝不允许犯愚蠢的错误，也不愿冒不必要的风险。要像蟒蛇一样紧紧缠住对手。在比赛最关键的时刻，当你有机会迈向 set point 时，一定要确保自己的状态完全掌控，思维也必须清晰正确。

## 11 7\. Closing Out a Match

>11 7\. 收官一局

It may seem out of place to include tactics for closing out a match in a chapter called “The Seven Hidden Ad Points.” After all, what’s so hidden about the opportunity presented when you’re serving for the match? The reward is obvious: winning the match. While the reward is obvious, the dangers aren’t. Closing out a match is a delicate time for the player who has the chance to do it.

>在名为“七种隐藏的发球局”的一章中加入关于如何终结比赛的战术，似乎有些格格不入。毕竟，当你在发球局中争夺整场比赛的胜利时，这个机会还有什么隐藏的呢？奖励是显而易见的：赢得比赛。虽然奖励显而易见，但其中的危险却未必如此。对于有机会终结比赛的球员来说，这个阶段其实非常微妙。

One of two attitudes usually prevails in the recreational player at such moments: an assumption that the job is almost done and victory is in hand, or a subtle fear that they won’t be able to finish the task.

>在这样的时刻，休闲球员通常有两种心态中的一种占据上风：一种是认为比赛已经接近尾声，胜利唾手可得；另一种则是隐隐约约的担忧，担心自己无法顺利完成比赛。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“recreational player”译为“休闲球员”而非“业余球员”，以更贴近原文语境中非职业选手的轻松氛围。

More dangerous than either of those mindsets is what is going on across the net with the player in danger of being closed out. One of the most common mistakes tennis players make is to underestimate the opponent who is in immediate danger of losing the match. It’s an extension of the Wounded Bear syndrome. That player is a lethal weapon. They will frequently play their best tennis just as you are in a position [[null|]]to win the match. Always remember: A fish fights hardest when you get it next to the boat! And a tennis player (at any level) does the same.

>比这两种心态更危险的是网对面那个濒临被终结比分的球员所处的境地。网球选手最常见的错误之一，就是低估了那个正处在输掉比赛边缘的对手。这正是“受伤熊综合征”的延伸。那个球员是一把致命武器，他们往往会在你即将赢得比赛的关键时刻，发挥出最佳水平。请永远记住：鱼儿在即将被拉上船边时，会奋力挣扎得最激烈！同样，任何水平的网球选手也都会如此。

Regardless of what they may have done previously in the match, expect the worst. This means expect their best. Assume they’re going to be faster and tougher, to hit deeper shots with fewer mistakes. They will fight their hardest as you try to drag them in.

>无论他们在比赛中之前表现如何，都要做好最坏的准备。这意味着要预设他们发挥出最佳状态。假设他们会更快、更顽强，击球更深且失误更少。当你试图将他们拉入泥潭时，他们会竭尽全力与你对抗。

>[!note]- 译注：此处“drag them in”意指让对手陷入被动局面，根据中文表达习惯稍作意译。

The way I prepare myself is to lie a little (again) to myself. I tell myself I’m the one in trouble. I’m the one who has to work to save the match. I’m the one who needs to be most alert. I want to feel that just when I’m closing in on victory I’m at the most dangerous point. I also remind myself to expect my opponent’s best tennis to surface at this time. I don’t want to be surprised by outstanding efforts.

>我准备自己的方式是对自己稍微撒点小谎（再次）。我告诉自己，是我在危险中，是我必须努力挽救比赛的人，是我必须最警惕的人。我想让自己感受到，就在我即将赢得比赛时，正是最危险的时刻。同时我也提醒自己，这个时候对手最出色的网球水平可能会突然展现出来。我不想被对手的出色表现所意外地击溃。

I’ll be sure to keep nerves under control by monitoring my breathing and footwork (Nerve Busters #1 and #2). D.R.M. is my tempo. I don’t want to drag along, but I want to be very sure that I’m mentally and emotionally under control before a point starts.

>我会通过监控自己的呼吸和步伐来保持冷静（神经杀手#1和#2）。D.R.M.是我的节奏。我不想拖泥带水，但在每一分开始前，我都希望确保自己在心理和情绪上完全掌控。

And when the point starts I return to my basic concept of winning tennis: no mistakes, no free points, no stupid shots. I want my opponent to get his points the hard way. I want him to earn them.

>当比赛开始后，我便回归自己最基本的网球取胜理念：不犯错误，不放过任何得分机会，不打愚蠢的球。我希望对手必须努力才能得分，我希望他靠实力赢得每一分。

## 12 Donate to Charity Not to Your Opponent!

>12 捐款给慈善机构，而不是你的对手！

One basic element of my approach to a tennis match (and especially to the Hidden Ad Points) is to be very stingy when it comes to giving my opponent free points. I work hard at managing my concentration and making sure I understand the dynamics of the match. The Seven Hidden Ad Points are recurring swing moments in the match where I want to be especially connected to what’s going on.

>我打网球（尤其是面对“隐藏发球分”时）的基本原则之一，就是尽可能少给对手“白送”的分数。我会努力保持专注，确保自己清楚比赛的动态。所谓的“七种隐藏发球分”，指的是比赛中反复出现的击球瞬间，我需要特别专注于当下发生的一切。

I want to make my opponent have to do something special to win the point or the game. I really batten down the hatches and try to produce my most focused thinking and smartest tennis. Is the first point of a game important? Yes. Is a game played at 3–2 important? Of course. All [[null|]]games are important. But for me the Seven Hidden Ad Points are the points that have the greatest potential for gain while being the most commonly overlooked or undervalued, especially among recreational players.

>我想让对手必须做些特别的事情才能赢得一分或一局。我真正全力以赴，集中精神，打出最聪明的网球。第一分是否重要？是的。比分3比2时的比赛是否重要？当然重要。每一局都很重要。但对我而言，七分关键分（Seven Hidden Ad Points）是那些最具潜力可赢、却最常被忽视或低估的得分，尤其是对于休闲球员来说更是如此。

If you recognize them as they occur in your matches and respond as I’ve suggested you will win more often. You’ll be taking advantage of the dynamic swing moments in the match. Improve your results there and you’ll improve your results when it comes to winning.

>如果你能在比赛中识别出这些情况，并按照我建议的方式做出反应，你就会赢得更多比赛。你将抓住比赛中的动态关键瞬间，提升这些时刻的表现，就能在赢得比赛方面取得更好的成绩。

Next: What to do when your shots fall apart.

>下一部分：当你的击球失误时该怎么办



# [[null|]][[null|]]10

>[[空|]][[空|]]10

# The Player’s Pit Stop: Stroke Repair

>球员的“补给站”：技术调整

Tour players who are ranked in the Top 20 or 25 play a few matches each year where they’re in the zone. I mean totally in the zone. When nobody on the planet is going to beat you on that day. When you feel no pressure and know you’ll win. When shots come off your racket with a sweetness and power that almost makes you laugh (or cry, because it doesn’t happen more often).

>排名在世界前20或前25的巡回赛选手，每年都会打几场比赛，那时他们完全进入状态。我是说，彻底进入状态。那种状态下，地球上没有人能打败你。你感觉不到任何压力，而且知道自己一定会赢。球拍击球时，球带着一种甜蜜与力量飞出，几乎让你忍不住笑出来（或者哭出来，因为这种情况并不多见）。

When it does happen you hope it happens in the finals of a grand slam event. It did for Sampras against Agassi in the ’90 U.S. Open. Nobody was going to beat Pete that day. And late at night over a cup of coffee he’ll tell you that. Michael Stich against Becker at Wimbledon in ’91. Boris could have stayed home, Stich was in the zone so deep.

>当这种情况发生时，你希望它发生在大满贯赛事的决赛中。萨姆普拉斯对阿加西就在1990年美国公开赛的决赛中就是这样。那天没人能击败皮特。深夜，他端着一杯咖啡，会这样告诉你。1991年温网，迈克尔·施蒂希对阵贝克尔，贝克尔本可以留在家里，施蒂希当时已经深入到“心流”状态。

Sometimes the zone lasts longer than one match. It happened for me during the summer of ’89. It started in West Germany where I won both my Davis Cup singles matches. I had just won the tournament in Memphis in the spring. Then I got into a serious zone. I won tournaments in Stratton Mountain, Vermont; Livingston, New Jersey; and Cincinnati. Along the way I defeated Jim Pugh, David Wheaton, Jim Courier, Boris Becker, Michael Chang, Pete Sampras, and Stefan Edberg. At one point my match record was 17 and 0. I became the first player since Becker in 1986 to win three consecutive tournaments. I was scorching the tour.

>有时候，这种“状态”会持续超过一场比赛。1989年夏天，我就经历过这种情况。那段时间，我从西德开始，连续赢下了两场戴维斯杯单打比赛。我刚刚在春天赢得了孟菲斯锦标赛的冠军。然后，我进入了一种非常专注的状态。我接连赢得了斯特拉顿山（Vermont）、利文斯顿（New Jersey）和辛辛那提的赛事冠军。在这期间，我击败了吉姆·普格（Jim Pugh）、大卫·惠顿（David Wheaton）、吉姆·库尔（Jim Courier）、博尔特·贝克尔（Boris Becker）、迈克尔·张（Michael Chang）、皮特·桑普拉斯（Pete Sampras）和斯蒂芬·埃德伯格（Stefan Edberg）。有一段时间，我的比赛战绩达到了17胜0负。我成为了自1986年贝克尔之后，首位连续赢得三项赛事冠军的球员。我当时简直势不可挡。

Then I went into the U.S. Open and lost in the first round. Nerves? No. Food poisoning. Some bad shellfish the night before I played Todd Witsken. It was bad luck, but I still stayed hot after the Open. Two [[null|]]weeks later I got into the finals in Los Angeles, and later I won the tournament in San Francisco. It was a phenomenal summer and an unforgettable year—five tournament victories plus the Davis Cup wins. That’s what you call really being in the zone. But it doesn’t happen often, and it usually doesn’t last that long.

>然后我参加了美国公开赛，结果第一轮就输了。不是紧张，是食物中毒。比赛前一天晚上吃了些不干净的海鲜，Todd Witsken是我那天的对手。这是运气不好，但我还是在美网之后保持了火热的状态。两周后我打进了洛杉矶的决赛，之后又在旧金山赢得了比赛。那是一个非常精彩的夏天，也是一个难以忘怀的一年——五座冠军奖杯加上戴维斯杯的胜利。这就是所谓的真正进入“心流”状态。但这种情况并不多见，而且通常也不会持续那么久。

## 1 The No-Zone: What to Do With Dog Meat

>1 无区地带：如何处理狗肉 

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“dog meat”为比喻用法，指代那些在比赛中被忽视或不被重视的球员或战术区域，而非字面意义上的“狗肉”。

Usually when a match is underway there is an ebb and flow to the quality of your play. It’s true for everyone at all levels of tennis. The dynamics are changing constantly. A single player rarely performs at their highest level of play (in the zone) for the whole contest. Your game varies in effectiveness and reliability. Sometimes you’re seeing and hitting the ball just fine. Then suddenly the wheels come off some part of your game and you’re dog meat.

>通常在一场网球比赛进行中，你的表现质量会有起有落。无论你在哪个水平层次，这一点都是真实的。比赛的节奏不断变化，单一选手很难在整个比赛中都处于最佳状态（即“进入心流”）。你的表现时而有效、可靠，时而却突然某方面出了问题，你顿时就像被“宰了的狗”一样。

This book isn’t aimed at improving your strokes. Go to a good teaching pro for that. They can see exactly what your particular problem is. They can evaluate your swing and give you specific ideas on how to improve. I want to give you some tips on what you can do during a match when a particular stroke suddenly goes sour. It may be that you start faulting on your first serve. Maybe your forehand groundstrokes are falling short or being netted.

>这本书并不是教你如何提高击球技术。如果你想要改善击球动作，去找一位专业的教练吧。他们能准确地发现你技术上的具体问题，评估你的击球动作，并给出具体的改进建议。我想说的是，在比赛中，当你某一击球技术突然失常时，你该怎么做。也许你一发球就开始出错，也许你的正手底线球频频不到位或触网。

Whatever the problem is it’s good to have an idea or mental image you can use to bring that stroke back to life before it costs you the match. These are tips that have worked for me over the years and have been effective for the players at my tennis camps. But like so many tips you read or hear about, some will work for your game and some may not. The next time the wheels come off try these and see if they help.

>无论你遇到什么问题，提前有一个想法或心理图像，可以帮助你让这项技术重新焕发生机，避免它让你在比赛中失利。这些都是我多年来在网球训练营中使用并证明有效的技巧，但就像你读到或听到的许多建议一样，有些对你适用，有些可能不适用。下一次当你技术出现失误时，不妨试试这些方法，看看是否有所帮助。

## 2 The Failing Forehand

>2 落后的正手击球

If there is one stroke the majority of recreational tennis players feel comfortable with it’s their forehand groundstroke. It may not be great, but [[null|]]it’s greater than the rest of their shots. You run around your backhand to hit it. You stay away from the net to hit it. You’d eat breakfast with it if you could. So when it gets wobbly you’re in trouble.

>大多数休闲网球选手最舒服的击球方式，莫过于他们的正手底线击球。它可能并不出色，但[[null|]]至少比他们其他击球方式要好。你绕到反手位去击打它，你远离网前去击打它，如果你能的话，你甚至会和它一起吃早餐。所以，一旦这个击球变得不稳定，你就麻烦了。

BETTER LATE THAN NEVER? WRONG!

>晚做总比不做好？错了！

There are a lot of things that can go wrong with any stroke, and the forehand is no exception. Without question the most stabilizing thing you can do to restore it when it gets in trouble is to check out your racket preparation. Are you getting your racket back in time? Probably not. More than likely you’re taking the racket back late. And the reason is usually understandable. We tend to get casual or careless on those physical movements that we’re comfortable with. Hey, we know that we can hit the shot with our forehand. No sweat.

>任何击球动作都可能出现各种问题，正手击球也不例外。毫无疑问，当正手击球出现问题时，最能稳定局势的做法就是检查你的挥拍准备动作。你是否在合适的时间把球拍回位了？很可能不是。更有可能的是，你是在太晚的时候才开始回拍。而原因通常也很容易理解。我们往往在那些自己感觉很熟练的动作上变得随意或粗心大意。嘿，我们知道自己可以用正手打出这记球，这不算什么难题。

When you take the racket back late (when the ball is almost on you) everything else in the swing is thrown off—footwork, balance, timing, and options. This can happen because of carelessness, casualness, fatigue, or the other player’s forcing shot. When you suddenly find yourself missing that forehand, focus immediately on an earlier takeaway.

>当你回拍动作太晚（球几乎已经来到你面前时），整个击球动作都会被打乱——脚步、平衡、节奏和击球选择。这种情况可能是因为粗心、随意、疲劳，或者对手的强力击球造成的。当你突然发现自己打不到那个正手击球时，立刻把注意力集中在更早的回拍动作上。

“IT’S AT THE NET. AM I READY YET?”

>“现在到了网前。我准备好了吗？”

The racket should be back when the tennis ball coming toward you is at the net. When that ball crosses the net you should be ready. Can you take the racket back too early? Maybe. But better too early than too late. For every player who takes the racket back too soon I see a hundred who take it back too late. When your match is under way and suddenly you find yourself cussing at your forehand, say to yourself, “It’s at the net. Am I ready yet?”

>球拍应该在网球朝你飞来、即将到达网前时才后摆。当球越过网时，你应当已经准备好。你是不是会过早地将球拍后摆？也许会。但与其过晚，不如过早。我看到的每一个过早回拍的球员，往往都有一百个是过晚才回拍的。当你比赛进行中，突然发现自己对着正手抱怨时，不妨对自己说：“球到网前了，我准备好了吗？”

## 3 Backhand Blues

>3 反手的烦恼

Most recreational players have low expectations for their backhand groundstrokes. They expect a certain (modest) level of production and are willing to tolerate mistakes, up to a point. That point differs from [[null|]]player to player, but it usually ends up with this statement uttered in total frustration: “I know I haven’t got much of a backhand, but this is ridiculous! ” It’s the backhand blues. Some C level players have such a poor backhand they can’t even tell when it goes bad. That’s the exception, however.

>大多数休闲球员对自己反手底线击球的期望都很低。他们预期一种（相对而言）平平的水平，并且愿意接受一定范围内的失误，但也有底线。这个底线因人而异，但最终往往会演变成一种彻底的沮丧情绪：“我知道我的反手不算好，但这也太离谱了！”这就是所谓的“反手忧郁症”。有些C级水平的球员，反手技术实在太差，甚至无法察觉自己的反手出了问题。不过，这种情况只是个例。

When your backhand gets so bad you’re running around it even to pick up a towel, it’s fix-up time. The most useful checkpoint I have concerns how much you’re trying to accomplish with your backhand groundstroke.

>当你反手打得如此糟糕，连捡毛巾都要绕着跑时，就该着手修复了。对我而言最有用的检查点之一，就是你用反手底线球想要完成多少事情。

DON’T ASK A SKINNY DOG TO FLY

>别让瘦狗飞天 

>[!note]- 译注：此句为习语，意指不要让能力不足的人去做力所不及的事，此处用“瘦狗”比喻能力有限的球员，强调不要让实力不足的选手去挑战强敌，否则只会吃苦头。

We all have a tendency to ask for more than a shot can give us. With the backhand groundstroke, asking for even a little more than it can give is usually a mistake. Recreational tennis players with a questionable backhand (if yours is solid, congratulations) tend to try to do too much with it, especially under pressure.

>我们总有一种倾向，就是对某一分的期望超过了它所能给予的。在反手底线击球时，哪怕只是稍微多一点的期望，通常都是一种错误。那些反手技术存疑的休闲球员（如果你的反手技术扎实，那恭喜你）往往会在压力下试图用反手做太多事情。

As I mentioned in chapter 8 (Destroying Your Opponent’s Game Plan) it’s very effective to come to the net against a weak backhand simply because a common reaction by the other player is to panic, to try and hit that darn backhand better than they’ve ever hit it in their life. Result? The attacking player didn’t even need to bring their racket to the net. The opponent’s backhand self-destructs.

>正如我在第八章（摧毁对手的比赛计划）中提到的，面对一个弱的反手，主动上网是一种非常有效的策略，因为对方常见的反应往往是惊慌失措，试图把那个该死的反手打得比他们一生中任何时候都好。结果呢？进攻一方甚至不需要把球拍拿到网前，对手的反手就已经自我毁灭了。

When your backhand starts to hurt you more than it usually does, lower your expectations. Stop trying to do more with it than you can reasonably expect. Get it over the net. Keep the ball in play. Go for placement instead of power. Keep your head when your backhand is under attack. Make your shot and force your opponent to at least make a play on it.

>当你反手开始比平时更让你吃力时，就降低你的期望。不要试图让它做它本来无法胜任的事情。把球打过网，保持球在场内。追求落点而非力量。当你的反手受到攻击时，要保持冷静。果断击球，迫使对手至少做出一次防守或进攻动作。

If I put you in front of a ball machine and said to just hit backhands over the net and in the court you’d do okay. Why? Because you’d be just trying to hit the ball over the net and into the court. When your backhand bites you during a match, remember that goal. Hit the ball over the net and into the court. Make that the goal. You’ll achieve it and the backhand will start to improve.

>如果你让我把你放在球机面前，只要求你不停地把反手球打过网落在场内，你也会做得不错。为什么？因为你只是在努力把球打过网落在场内。当你在比赛中遭遇反手失误时，记住这个目标。把球打过网落在场内。让这个目标成为你的指引。你将会实现它，反手技术也会随之逐渐提升。

## 4 [[null|]]Your Serve Goes South

>4 你的发球出问题了

When the serve disappears it’s the most frustrating of all stroke breakdowns because you can’t really blame anyone but yourself for the trouble. When your backhand, forehand, volley, or overhead come apart at least you can look over the net and blame it on your opponent. They had to hit the ball before you could screw up, right? Not with the serve. All they did was stand there. Tough to blame them for your double fault when they’re just standing there.

>当发球失误时，这是所有击球失误中最令人沮丧的一种，因为除了你自己，你无法责怪任何人。当你的反手、正手、截击或过顶击球出问题时，你至少还能跨过网线，把责任归咎于对手。他们必须先击球，你才有可能搞砸，对吧？但发球就不同了。他们只是站在那儿。在他们只是站着不动的时候，你又能怎么责怪他们造成双误呢？

(Note: I don’t underestimate the effect that “just standing there” can have. Don’t forget Chang beat Lendl in the quarters of the French Open by “just standing there.” On match point Michael was cramping up so bad he could hardly move. To cut off Lendl’s serving angles Chang camped on the service line. The mighty Lendl collapsed. He double-faulted his way out of the French Open. It was an unbelievable tactical move that had an unbelievable psychological effect. So there are exceptions, but generally you’ve got nobody to blame for your service fault but you.)

>（注：我并不低估“站在原地不动”这种做法的效果。别忘了，在法网四分之一决赛中，张德培就是靠“站在原地不动”击败了莱德利普。到了决胜分，迈克尔的腿部抽筋严重，几乎无法移动。为了截断莱德利普的发球角度，张德培干脆站在发球线上。强大的莱德利普最终崩溃了，他连丢两个发球局，惨败出局。这是一次令人难以置信的战术举动，也产生了难以想象的心理影响。所以，确实有例外，但一般来说，你自己的发球失误只能怪自己。）

LOOK IN THE MIRROR—DO YOU SEE PETE SAMPRAS?

>照照镜子——你看到皮特·桑普拉斯了吗？

Start correcting the problem during a match by remembering this. Your best serve may not be as good as you think it is. It isn’t a cannon. It isn’t an ace machine. And it isn’t worth double-faulting for. And that’s what you risk doing. Most recreational players (especially guys) believe if they can get everything right on the toss, the extension, the wrist snap, and the follow-through, they’ll have a super serve. So they pursue that elusive monster at their own expense.

>在比赛中发现问题时，就要立刻开始纠正。记住这一点：你最出色的发球可能并没有你想象中那么好。它不是一门大炮，也不是一台发ACE球的机器，它也不值得你为了它而犯双误。而你却冒着这样的风险去做。大多数休闲球员（尤其是男性）都相信，只要他们在抛球、伸展、手腕发力和收势这些环节都做到位，就一定能打出一记超级发球。因此，他们不惜一切代价去追求那个遥不可及的“怪物”发球。

Here’s an indication of how it works. At the recreational level a very common time to double-fault is after a service ace. Reason? The player who serves up that ace loves it and figures the puzzle is solved. “Hey, I’ve got it working now!” Bang. Fault. Bang. Fault. Double fault after the ace. Which was the accident, the double fault or the ace?

>这能说明这种现象是如何发生的。在休闲水平的比赛中，一个非常常见的双误（double fault）发生时间是在发球直接得分（ace）之后。原因是什么呢？打出这个ace的发球手非常喜欢这个结果，认为问题已经解决了。“嘿，我这下搞定了！”砰！失误。砰！失误。在ace之后出现双误。那么，究竟是这个ace，还是这个双误是意外呢？

My suggestion is to get a realistic view of your serve. As for my own [[null|]]serve, I occasionally get my first working and it can spit out a few aces. But a lot of the time I know I have to manage it. It isn’t going to overpower my opponent and I hate donating points. So I keep a realistic view of what I can accomplish with my first serve. And I’ve told you how my second serve is—the worst. So I don’t get into a macho mindset of trying to show the other guy how “big” my serve is. And neither should you.

>我的建议是，要对你的发球有一个现实的认识。至于我自己的发球，我偶尔能发出第一发球并取得一些优势，偶尔还能打出一些ACE球。但很多时候我知道，我必须控制好它。它不可能压倒对手，我讨厌白白丢分。因此，我对自己第一发球能实现什么有着现实的认识。至于我的第二发球，我已经告诉过你了——那是最差的。因此，我不会陷入一种逞强的心态，试图向对方展示我的发球“多么强大”。你也应该如此。

DOWNSHIFT FROM FOURTH TO THIRD

>从第四档降档至第三档

When you start missing that first serve I want you to downshift. Let’s call your “maximum” serve fourth gear. That’s when you’re going full out and really taking a big cut at the ball. What usually happens is a player who is missing that serve will keep missing it because they don’t want to back away from the challenge. They keep banging their head against the wall time after time hoping the serve will come back. Forget it. Shift gears. Not from fourth to first suddenly, but from fourth to third. Downshift slightly. Don’t try to do as much. Don’t worry about the ace. Don’t worry about service winners. Worry about starting the point without a fault or double fault.

>当你开始发球频频出错时，我希望你立刻降档。我们把你的“最大”发球称为第四档，那是你全力以赴、全力击球的状态。通常发生的情况是，一个频频失误发球的球员会一直失误下去，因为他们不想退缩，不愿面对挑战。他们一次次地撞墙，希望发球能重新找回状态。别再这样了。换档，但不是从第四档突然降到第一档，而是从第四档降到第三档。稍微降档，不要求自己做太多。不要担心发ACE球，也不要太在意发球直接得分。你要担心的是，如何在不犯双误的情况下开始这个得分点。

Does that mean you should just bloop it over the net? No. That’s going all the way down to first gear. Remember when Mecir had all those double faults and started serving underhand? He went from fourth to first. Mentally, you should just drop it down to third gear. Get some balls in and some rhythm back. Then move back up to fourth. You’ll like the results.

>这是否意味着你只需要把球轻轻打过网？不，那样就降到一档了。还记得梅奇尔曾经连着出现双误，甚至开始用下手发球吗？他从四档直接降到了一档。从心理层面来说，你只需要降到三档。先多击几个球，找回节奏感。然后再慢慢升回四档。你一定会喜欢这样的效果。

## 5 The Vanishing Volley

>5 消失的截击球

The easier the volley is, the lazier the player gets. Watch the players at your courts. When anyone gets a “duck,” the kind of ball that’s just barely flapping its way over the net, they get lazy or passive. They wait for the ball to arrive. They don’t move forward. They assume it’s going to be easy. And of course they blow the shot. Usually with a huge last-second swipe at the ball that goes long, wide, or into the net.

>越简单的截击球，球员就越容易懈怠。去观察你身边球场上的球员吧。当有人拿到一个“鸭子球”——也就是刚刚好越过网线、轻轻晃荡着飞来的球时，他们往往会变得懒散或被动。他们等着球飞到面前，不主动向前移动，还自以为这球很容易处理。当然，他们最终往往会失误。通常是在最后一刻仓促挥拍，把球打飞出界、打偏或打进网里。

>[!note]- “鸭子球”是网球术语，指那种轻轻飘过网线、几乎不带旋转的球，常让球员放松警惕。

[[null|]]MOVE TO THE BALL

The closer you are to the net, the better your chance of making a successful volley—the net is less of a factor, you have better angles to use, and you have more of your opponent’s court to hit to. Never wait for the ball to arrive. This isn’t the Post Office. You don’t wait for delivery. In tennis you’ve got to go pick it up. And with a volley, that’s especially true. The quicker you pick it up the better. The extra step or two into the net will improve your percentage of successful volleys dramatically.

>你越靠近网前，就越有可能打出成功的截击球——网对你的影响越小，你拥有的击球角度也越好，而且你有更多的对手场区可以击球。不要等待球飞到你面前。这不是邮局，你不能等着别人来送信。在网球比赛中，你必须主动去“捡球”。而截击球更是如此。你越快去击球，成功率就越高。多向前跨出一步或两步靠近网前，将极大地提高你成功截击球的百分比。

So as you’re going in to hit a volley, get close to the net. Every step you take closer to it improves your chance of success. Watch John McEnroe or Stefan Edberg. Both of them close out points by getting so close to the net they could lick it. And they do it with great swiftness, like a hawk swooping down on its prey.

>所以，当你准备击球上网时，尽量靠近网线。每靠近一步，你成功的几率就增加一分。看看约翰·麦肯罗或斯蒂芬·埃德伯格，他们总是通过迅速接近网线来结束得分，近到几乎能舔到网线。他们像老鹰俯冲猎物一样迅速而果断。

## 6 The Underachieving Overhead

>6 拉球失误者

So you take my advice and now you’re on top of the net for those volleys. Only you’re not getting a chance to hit any volleys because your opponent realizes you’re up so close even rimshots off your racket can dribble over the net for winners. So they start lobbing you and now it’s your overhead that is missing in action. You’re snapping them into the net. You’re pushing them deep. They’re going so wide they’d be out even if you were playing doubles.

>所以你按照我的建议去做，现在你已经站在网前准备接那些截击球了。但问题是，你根本没有机会打出任何截击球，因为你的对手已经意识到你离球网太近了，就连你 racket 边缘的擦网球都能滚过网去，直接得分。于是他们开始大力上旋球，现在你原本赖以得分的正手高球却完全派不上用场。你频频把球打到网里，你不断把球打到对方底线附近，他们打得那么宽，就算你打双打，他们也早就出界了。

GO FOR PLACEMENT

>争取位置 

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“placement”指击球时球拍击球点的位置，译为“位置”更符合中文表达习惯。

When that happens it’s because you are usually thinking “power” instead of “placement.” Most of the time when an overhead is coming toward you the goal becomes to end the point, to hit an outright winner. Again, it’s the trap of asking more from a shot than one can reasonably expect it to give. If your overhead gets shaky during a match, you’ve got to regroup. Don’t try to do so much with it. Resist thinking, “I’ve got to end it.” Go for placement instead of power. You’ll have immediate results [[null|]]because you’ve taken the pressure of hitting hard off your swing. It will be more rhythmic, more loose, and much more effective.

>当这种情况发生时，通常是因为你脑子里想的是“力量”而不是“落点”。大多数时候，当对手的反手击球朝你飞来时，你的目标应该是结束这一分，打出一个直接得分的球。然而，这又是一个常见的陷阱——对一记击球寄予了它无法合理承担的期望。如果你在比赛中反手击球变得不稳定，你必须迅速调整心态。不要试图用这记球做太多事情。不要想着“我必须结束比赛”。应该追求落点而非力量。这样你马上就能看到效果，因为你在击球时已经把对力量的过度依赖从挥拍中卸下。这会更富有节奏感，更放松，也更有效。

## 7 Playing in Wind

>7 风中作战

The wind can affect your strokes because it works on your mind. If you’re uncomfortable in the wind, here are some ideas that will help you neutralize its negative effects.

>风会影响你的击球，因为它作用于你的心理。如果你在风中感到不适，这里有一些方法可以帮助你抵消它的负面影响。

1\. START WITH THE WIND IN YOUR FACE

>1\. 逆风而行

Sun is the most important factor to consider when electing which end of the court to choose. As I mentioned in chapter 6, “The Smart Start,” if the sun is a problem I’ll start the match with it at my back so my opponent has to deal with it first. However, if the sun isn’t an issue (at night, or not in the line of sight) the wind is the next consideration. If it is blowing north to south (baseline to baseline) I will elect to start the match with it in my face. That first game is shaky enough without having the wind push my shots long. Hitting into the wind allows me to hit out and I have the assurance of the wind knocking the ball down a bit.

>太阳是决定选择球场哪一端的首要因素。正如我在第六章“聪明的开局”中提到的，如果阳光是个问题，我会选择让阳光从我背后照射进来，让对手先面对阳光。但如果阳光不是问题（比如在晚上，或者不在视线范围内），那么接下来就要考虑风向了。如果风是从北向南吹（即从底线吹向底线），我会选择让风迎面吹来。这样第一盘开局本身就够不稳了，如果再让风把我的球吹得过长，那就更难打了。逆风击球可以让我打得更有优势，而且我也有信心风会把球稍微压低一些。

2\. LOWER YOUR TOSS

>2\. 降低抛球高度

A tennis ball doesn’t weigh much. A windy day can make it seem like it’s a leaf blowing around, especially on your toss. If the wind starts to affect your serve, bring your toss down. Reduce its height a few inches (or more) and you reduce the wind’s effect.

>网球的重量并不大。在风天，它看起来就像一片随风飘荡的树叶，尤其是在你抛球的时候。如果风开始影响你的发球，就把抛球的动作降低一些。把抛球的高度减少几英寸（或更多），就能减少风的影响。

3\. SHORTEN YOUR STROKES

>3\. 缩短你的击球动作

The same goes for your groundstrokes when you’re playing in a real breeze. Try to make your shots more compact and concentrate on good contact. You’ll reduce the number of mishits and increase the number of shots that go back over the net on a windy day.

>你打底线球时也是一样，尤其是在有风的比赛中。试着让击球动作更紧凑，专注于击球点的控制。这样你就能减少失误次数，并在有风的日子里提高球过网的次数。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“mishits”译为“失误”更符合中文表达习惯，而非直译“击球失误”。

[[null|]]4\. THE BEST WEAPON AGAINST WIND

Finally, remember that if wind is making your tennis life miserable the ultimate wind cheater is this: Build your own indoor court. Then invite me over to play. I don’t like playing in wind either.

>最后，请记住，如果你觉得风让你的网球生活变得很糟糕，那么终极的“风之作弊者”就是这个：打造属于自己的室内球场。然后邀请我来打球。我也不喜欢在风中打球。

## 8 A Final Fact About Footwork

>8 关于步法的最后一条事实

Tips are tips. You’ll find one in Tennis magazine that works for you and you’ll tell a friend. It won’t do anything for them. Players differ so much in their physical skills, the amount of time they play and practice, and their motivation level that it’s rare that a tip will help everyone. But there is one tip I’ll give you (again) that does work for everyone. It’s this: Good footwork improves your tennis.

>技巧就是技巧。你可以在《网球杂志》上找到一条适合你的技巧，然后告诉朋友。但这条技巧对朋友未必有用。球员在身体素质、打球和练习时间以及动机水平方面差异很大，因此很少有一条技巧能对所有人都起作用。不过，我会再告诉你一条（其实我之前已经说过）适用于所有人的技巧。那就是：良好的步法能提升你的网球水平。

All of the problems you face with strokes have many solutions. But the first and most important thing to check is your footwork. If it’s bad it can hurt every shot you hit. Or, it can improve every shot you hit. Whenever you start having a problem with any shot, check your footwork. You know how to do it: get on your toes (the balls of your feet). If you stay light and on your toes you will increase your chances for good stroke execution significantly.

>你面对所有击球问题时，其实有很多解决办法。但首先要检查的是你的步法。如果步法不好，它会毁掉你击出的每一个球；或者，它也能提升你击出的每一个球。每当你在某一个击球动作上出现问题时，首先就要检查你的步法。你已经知道该怎么做：要站上脚尖（脚掌部位）。如果你能保持轻盈并站上脚尖，你击球的成功率将大幅提升。

## 9 Practice Doesn’t Make Perfect, but It Helps

>9 拼命练习不等于完美，但能有所帮助

The real key to improving any of your strokes is to work on them when you’re not playing a match. Most players think they’ll get better if they just play tennis. They play and play and never can figure out why they don’t improve. Practice may not make it perfect, but it sure makes it better.

>提升任何击球技术的关键，其实是在比赛之外进行练习。大多数球员认为只要多打网球，技术自然就会进步。他们不断打球，却始终搞不清楚为什么自己没有进步。练习或许无法让技术完美，但它一定能让技术变得更好。

In golf if all you do is play and never hit a shot out of a sand trap except during the round, you won’t get better at sand shots. In fact, you’ll probably get worse because as you miss some you’ll start to get nervous about the shot.

>在高尔夫球中，如果你只是打球，除了在比赛中偶尔从沙坑中击球外，从不练习沙坑击球，那你永远无法提高沙坑击球的技术。事实上，你可能会越打越差，因为当你一次次失误时，你会开始对这一击感到紧张。

>[!note]- 译注：此处强调的是专项训练的重要性，避免因缺乏练习而产生的心理压力。

[[null|]]PRACTICE LIKE JACK NICKLAUS

The greatest golfer in the history of the game may also have been the greatest practicer in the history of the game. He practiced with a purpose. He knew what he wanted to work on and he isolated it on the practice range. He was very methodical about fixing the problems that occurred during a match by addressing them in his practice session.

>历史上最伟大的高尔夫球手也许也是这项运动历史上最刻苦的练习者。他练习时目标明确，知道自己要改进什么，并在练习场上有针对性地进行训练。他在比赛中出现的问题，也会在练习中一一解决，整个过程非常有条理。

You can make a great improvement in your tennis game by doing the same. Working on a specific problem even for thirty minutes once a month will give you terrific results. If you can do it twice a month you won’t believe what can happen.

>你也可以通过同样方法大幅提升自己的网球水平。即使每月只花三十分钟专门解决某个问题，你也会取得惊人的进步。如果你能每月做两次，你将难以想象会发生多么大的变化。

How to Improve?

>如何提高？

1\. Check on swing mechanics by taking a lesson. Your club pro will get you swinging correctly.

>1\. 检查挥拍技术，上一堂课。你的球杆教练会帮你纠正挥拍动作。

>[!note]- 译注：此处“club pro”指的是高尔夫球杆教练，若读者对网球不熟悉，可译为“教练”或“专业教练”。

2\. Practice what you learned during the lesson. Use a ball machine, the backboard, or a wall. Don’t just flail away without a plan. Start by swinging easily and go for consistency. Play little games with yourself. Try to hit the shot you’re working on two times in a row. Then three times in a row. Isolate it and concentrate on it. When I was a kid I spent hours and hours hitting against backboards and walls in Piedmont, California. I would play entire imaginary matches in the U.S. Open against an imaginary Ilie Nastase. The wall was Nastase and it was great practice because the wall would never miss.

>2\. 把你在课堂上学到的东西付诸实践。使用球机、后墙或者墙壁来练习。不要毫无计划地乱打一通。首先，轻松地挥拍，注重稳定性。你可以和自己玩一些小比赛。尝试连续两次击中你正在练习的球拍动作，然后再连续三次。把注意力集中在这个动作上，单独练习。我小时候在加州皮德蒙特，花了很多小时对着后墙和墙壁击球。我还会在美网的想象中和一个虚构的伊莱·纳斯塔塞进行整场比赛。那面墙就是纳斯塔塞，这种练习非常棒，因为墙壁从不失误。

3\. Play someone you know you can beat without much trouble. Look for opportunities during the match to work on the shot that you practiced against the backboard. You may lose. Don’t worry about it.

>3\. 找一个你清楚自己可以轻松击败的对手。在比赛中寻找机会，去练习你之前在墙上练习过的那个球技。你可能会输，但不要担心。

If your backhand is weak, make sure that you never run around it in this practice match. If your backhand volley is in question, look for chances to hit it. Club players don’t like to do this because they’re afraid their friends will find out about the results. Don’t let your ego get in the way of progress. You’ll be winning points from those same friends with what you’ve improved.

>如果你的反手较弱，那么在这次练习赛中，**千万不要绕着反手跑**。如果你的反手截击技术有问题，那就**主动寻找机会去击球**。普通业余球手通常不喜欢这么做，因为他们担心自己的朋友会知道结果。**不要让自尊心阻碍你的进步**。你通过提升反手所赢得的分数，**正是来自那些朋友**。

[[null|]]4\. Bring the shot into your regular matches. You’ll find that instead of expecting difficulties on the weak stroke, you’ll be looking at it with more and more confidence. Both your shot and your attitude about the shot will be better.

5\. Play against someone who is better than you are, who will beat you. Playing your buddies all the time gets you into the habit of putting your mind and your game on automatic pilot. Go against someone better and you’ve got to dig down inside yourself. You’ve got to work harder, think more, run more, and you’re still going to lose. Great. That’s why you’re there. It’ll pay off when you go back to your regular opponents.

>5\. 与比你强的人比赛，他们最终会打败你。如果你总是和朋友比赛，就会养成一种习惯，把你的思维和打法都放到自动模式上。而当你面对比你更强的对手时，你就必须深入挖掘自己的潜力。你必须更加努力地训练、更加用心地思考、更加拼命地奔跑，即使你还是输了。很好，这就是你来这里的原因。当你回到平时的对手身上时，这些努力都会得到回报。

A little attention in the form of practice will produce big results in your game. Winning is a lot more fun than losing, and improving your weakest areas will make winning easier.

>一点点的关注，以练习的形式呈现，会在你的比赛中带来巨大的成果。赢比输要有趣得多，而改善你最薄弱的环节会让赢变得更加轻松。

Next: Stealing from the superstars.

>下一部分：从超级明星身上“偷”技巧。



# [[null|]][[null|]]11

>[[null|]][[null|]]11

# Learning From the Legends

>从传奇人物身上学习

The superstars of tennis exhibit physical skills that are almost uncanny. In his prime, John McEnroe’s eye-hand coordination was equal to any athlete in the world—if you’ve ever watched a cat’s paw toy with a ball of string (or a mouse), John’s hand on a racket had the same delicate grace and deadly purpose. Boris Becker’s overwhelming physicality would make him a superstar in almost any sport he chose. Early in his career when he was diving after shots he almost made tennis a contact sport. Boris as a star quarterback, home run king, or basketball hero? No problem. And what about Andre Agassi? How can a player take the ball that early and hit it that hard? His timing is better than a Rolex. The same level of outrageous physical gifts applies to all the great ones: Sampras, Edberg, Connors, and others.

>网球巨星们展现出的体能技巧几乎令人难以置信。在巅峰时期，约翰·麦肯罗的眼手协调能力可媲美世界上任何运动员——如果你曾经见过猫爪玩线团（或逗弄老鼠），那么约翰挥拍时的手腕便拥有同样细腻优雅且致命的精准。博格斯·贝克尔那压倒性的身体素质，让他几乎能在任何运动中成为巨星。在他职业生涯初期，他为了接球甚至会扑向球，那时的网球几乎变成了接触性运动。如果博格斯是足球场上的明星四分卫、棒球赛场上的全垒打王，或是篮球场上的英雄，又有什么问题呢？至于安德烈·阿加西，他是如何能在如此早的击球点将球击得如此有力？他的时机把握比劳力士手表还要精准。这种夸张的体能天赋，同样适用于所有伟大的球员：桑普拉斯、埃德伯格、康纳斯，以及其他许多球员。

So, can you learn anything from them? After all, they’re blessed with physical gifts most people only dream about. You can’t “learn” a natural gift can you? Yes, you can, but not necessarily in the way you think. Obviously, certain mechanical fundamentals apply to all levels of tennis—turn your shoulders, use your legs, keep your eyes on the ball. All stuff you’ve heard before.

>所以，你能从他们身上学到什么吗？毕竟，他们拥有大多数人只能梦想拥有的身体天赋。你难道能“学会”一种天生的才能吗？是的，你可以，但不是你想象的那种方式。显然，某些基本的技术要领适用于所有水平的网球选手——转动肩膀、运用腿部力量、眼睛盯着球。这些都是你以前就听过的老生常谈。

I’d like you to think about a different area when it comes to learning from these tennis superstars. It is this: their attitude and tactics during a match and how these apply to your tennis.

>我想让你从另一个角度来思考如何从这些网球巨星身上学习。这个角度是：他们在比赛中的态度和战术，以及这些如何应用到你的网球实战中。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“attitude and tactics”翻译为“态度和战术”，既保留了原文的含义，也符合中文表达习惯。

Keep in mind that very few rules apply to everyone. What works for you may not work for someone else. As you think about what these superstars bring to their game remember they’ve often succeeded with totally different approaches. Study what they do and [[null|]]look for what can help your own approach, given your style of play and temperament.

>请记住，很少有一套规则适用于所有人。对你有效的方法，可能对别人却不起作用。在思考这些超级明星如何为他们的比赛带来优势时，请记住他们往往通过截然不同的方式取得成功。研究他们所做的一切，[[null|]]并寻找那些能够帮助你根据自己的打法和性格特点，完善自身策略的方法。

## 1 Andre Agassi

>1 安德烈·阿加西

It’s showtime when Double A arrives. Neon clothes. Neon hair. He’s like a rock star. He gets away with it because when it comes to tennis he delivers the product.

>双A登场，好戏开场。霓虹色的服装，霓虹色的头发，他就像一位摇滚明星。他之所以能这么张扬，是因为在网球赛场上，他始终能交出令人满意的答卷。

>[!note]- “Double A”为网球选手的昵称，此处保留英文原名以保持人物特色。

I’ve never seen a guy his size get so much stick on the ball. It’s really unbelievable. He’s just got serious heat. Because of it, he puts immediate fear into you because you know he can just rack the ball and control play. When he’s on his game, he just moves you back and forth at will. It’s no fun to play Andre when he’s “on.”

>我从未见过一个体型这么大的球员能像他这样把球打得这么有威胁。这简直难以置信。他现在压力真的很大。正因为如此，他一上场就让你感到害怕，因为你清楚他只要一发力就能把球打得又高又远，完全掌控比赛节奏。当他状态好的时候，他能随心所欲地把对手来回调动。跟他打的时候，如果他“在状态”，那就真的没什么乐趣可言了。

He also is a guy who plays on emotion. If he’s feeling mentally, emotionally, and physically good, and things are working for him, he is definitely the best player in the world. (Except for Jim Courier, who when he’s “on” is also the best in the world. Two best in the worlds? Right. I think that one of the great rivalries of the ’90s is going to be Agassi and Courier, two phenomenal athletes who go back a long way with each other. They battled when they were Juniors and then at Nick Bolletieri camps. On the court against each other they take no prisoners. When they meet in the finals of a Slam event—and I don’t think it will be long from now—be sure you stop whatever you’re doing and watch it on the tube. There’ll be blood on the tracks when they’re done with each other.)

>他也是一个靠情绪打球的人。如果他在心理、情绪和身体状态上都感觉良好，一切顺利，那他绝对是世界上最好的球员。（当然，还有吉姆·科里尔，当他状态巅峰时，也绝对是世界顶级。两个世界第一？对。我认为90年代最伟大的对决之一，将是阿加西和科里尔之间的较量。这两位非凡的运动员彼此相识已久，他们从小一起参加青少年比赛，后来又在尼克·波利泰里尼的训练营中交手。在球场上，他们从不手软，彼此之间毫不留情。当他们在大满贯决赛中相遇——我想不会太久就会发生——请务必停下你正在做的事情，打开电视观看。他们交手之后，场上定会血迹斑斑。）

One of Andre’s greatest assets is his ability to take the ball extremely early, on the rise. Connors has also done that throughout his career, but Andre takes it even earlier and hits it harder. The way he does it is almost impossible to copy or more pros would. Many times his groundstrokes are virtually a half-volley, he takes it so close to the bounce. However, the basic idea is something you should keep in mind for your own game.

>安德烈最大的优势之一，就是他能够在球还在上升时就非常早地击球。康纳斯在他的职业生涯中也一直采用这种打法，但安德烈击球更早，击球力量也更大。他这样击球的方式，几乎让其他职业选手难以模仿。很多时候，他的正手击球几乎就像是半高球，因为他几乎在球触地的瞬间就击球了。不过，这个基本理念是你在自己的比赛中应该牢记的。

Taking the ball early means sending it back to your opponent harder and sooner. It’s devastating to hit a shot to Andre and have him blast it [[null|]]back to you before you’ve even finished your swing. It seems like it happens that quickly. Your own opponents won’t like seeing the ball come back at them sooner either.

>提前击球意味着更早、更用力地将球回击给对手。当你击球到安德烈身上，而他几乎在你挥拍动作还没完成时就将球狠狠回击到你这边，这种情形简直令人崩溃。看起来这一切发生得如此之快。你的对手看到球更早地飞回他们那边，也不会感到高兴。

For your own game don’t think about hitting the ball early. Think about hitting it earlier. Normally you’d wait for the tennis ball to land on your side of the court, bounce, rise, and start to fall before you hit it, below the top of its arc. That’s because it’s easier to hit that way; it’s moving slower and you’ve had more time to get to it. But that strategy also gives your opponent more time to get set, attack, or recover. It also means you have to swing harder to create pace or get depth because the ball is losing speed by the time you hit it.

>在你的比赛中，不要想着提早击球，而要想着更早击球。通常情况下，你会等网球落到你这边场地后弹起、上升，再开始下落时才击球，这时球还在其最高点的下方。这是因为这种方式击球更容易，球此时移动较慢，你也有更多时间去到达击球点。但这种策略也给了对手更多时间来准备、进攻或恢复。此外，这也意味着你必须挥拍更用力才能打出速度或深度，因为球在你击打时已经减速了。

So think “earlier” instead of “early.” Here’s how to start.

>所以，要想到“更早”而不是“早”。下面是开始的方法。

When you get a ball that’s coming deep to you the natural tendency is to back up and wait for the ball to drop before you hit it. Instead, force yourself to move into the ball and take it just slightly earlier—10 percent earlier. When practicing make it a goal. Look for balls that you might otherwise be a little lazy on. Step into them and hit 10 percent sooner than you normally would after they start descending.

>当你接到来球非常深时，你的本能反应是往后退一步，等球下落一点再击球。但相反，你要强迫自己主动向前迎球，提前一点点——提前10%。在练习时，把这当作一个目标。寻找那些你原本可能会有些懒惰的球，主动上前击球，比你通常习惯的提前10%去击球，当球开始下落时就立即行动。

Get used to it and then start looking for an opportunity to take the ball right at the top of its arc. Now you’ll see some results (both good and bad). You’ll have your share of mishit balls, but as you get comfortable with taking the ball earlier you’ll see it go back harder, deeper, and faster.

>习惯这种感觉，然后开始寻找机会，在球到达最高点时击球。现在你将会看到一些效果（有好有坏）。你可能会有一些击球失误，但随着你逐渐适应提前击球的感觉，你会发现球回弹得更重、更远、更快。

The other thing to notice about Andre when you watch him play is the way his feet and racket are moving together at all times. They don’t move separately and neither should yours. Don’t move your feet and then suddenly jerk your racket into position. Bad timing is guaranteed. That’s a pretty basic idea, but Andre really is the best example of how to do it. When you see him play on television watch that great early racket preparation.

>当你观看阿加西比赛时，另一个值得注意的地方是他的双脚与球拍始终协调一致地移动。它们不会各自分开移动，你的双脚和球拍也应如此。不要先移动双脚，然后再突然把球拍猛地摆到正确位置。这样的时机把握很差，注定会失败。这其实是一个相当基本的概念，但阿加西确实是这方面的最佳示范。当你在电视上看他比赛时，注意他那出色的早期球拍准备动作。

When Andre swings wide to either side his racket moves back almost immediately. When he is receiving serve his racket moves back as soon as the server makes contact with the ball. It’s why he can take the ball so early and with such precision—his racket preparation is excellent. It’s unsurpassed on the tour.

>当安德烈的球拍向左右两侧挥动时，他的球拍几乎立刻就会回到原位。他在接发球时，球拍也几乎在发球手触球的瞬间就回到准备位置。这正是他能如此早且精准地击球的原因——他的球拍准备动作非常出色。在巡回赛中，这种准备动作是无人能及的。

[[null|]]The Lesson From Agassi

1\. Practice taking the ball 10 percent earlier for more damaging groundstrokes.

>1\. 练习提前10%击球，以打出更具破坏力的底线击球。

2\. Move your racket and your feet simultaneously.

>2\. 同时移动球拍和双脚。

The results will show up in your scores. Who knows, you may even start wanting to bleach your hair. Believe me, if I thought it would give me Agassi’s groundstrokes I’d do it.

>你的成绩会如实反映出来。谁知道呢，你甚至可能开始想漂白头发。相信我，如果我认为这样能让我拥有阿加西式的底线击球，我早就做了。

## 2 Ivan Lendl

>2 伊万·伦德尔

Ivan Lendl hits the ball harder and with more accuracy than any player on the planet. He just knocks the cover off the ball. The major difference between him and Agassi is that Ivan is usually four or five feet behind the baseline when he makes contact. Andre is often inside the baseline so his shot gets to you sooner and is going faster. But there are three other elements of the Terminator’s game that you might want to incorporate into your own approach.

>伊万·伦德尔击球的力量和准确性无人能及，他几乎能把球拍打到球的最远点。他与阿加西之间的主要区别在于，伊万通常在底线后四到五英尺的地方击球，而阿加西则常常在底线前击球，因此他的球到达你面前更快，也更具速度。不过，还有三项“终结者”打法的要素，你也可以考虑融入自己的打法中。

First of all, Ivan is known for his consistency. It is something he is careful to establish at the very beginning of a match. As I mentioned, when he comes out and begins the first several games he will not miss a ball. That’s because he’s hitting at only 65 percent to 70 percent of his full power. You should approach the beginning of your own matches the same way. Set your timing, rhythm, and confidence in place before going for more power.

>首先，伊万以稳定著称。这是他在比赛一开始就特别注重建立的东西。正如我之前所说，当他上场开始前几个发球局时，他几乎不会失分，这是因为他的击球力量只达到满力的65%到70%。你应该以同样的方式面对自己比赛的开局。在追求更强力量之前，先建立好节奏、信心和时机。

Second, Ivan has a favorite little spot on the court that is sort of his own personal pitcher’s mound. Have you noticed how he likes to move about four feet left of center on the baseline? He is actually running around his backhand just slightly (sometimes more than just slightly). He just loves to park himself there and start cranking the forehand. From that spot he loves to move you back and forth as he opens up the court.

>第二，伊万有一个自己最喜欢的场地角落，有点像他个人的投手丘。你有没有注意到，他喜欢在底线中央左侧大约四英尺的位置移动？他实际上是在绕着自己的反手位轻轻跑动（有时甚至跑得更远）。他特别喜欢停在这个位置，然后开始大力挥动正手。从这个位置，他特别喜欢将你来回调动，从而打开场地。

When I’ve played him he’ll settle in on that spot and start moving me right and left, wider and wider. Finally, I’ll hit one short and he [[null|]]bangs out a winner. He feels very confident and strong in that position.

>每当我跟他比赛时，他都会先站定在那个位置，然后开始把我向左右、向更宽的范围调动。最后，我打出一个短球，他[[null|]]立刻轰出一记制胜球。他在那个位置上感觉非常自信和强大。

In your own game look for the spot on the court that gives you your favorite shot and work to get there. If you love the forehand, set up your own pitcher’s mound and fire away. If it’s the forehand volley, start really looking for opportunities to come to the net. Don’t wait for an invitation (a very weak shot). Force the issue a little.

>在你自己的比赛中，寻找球场上让你打出最喜爱击球的那个位置，并努力到达那里。如果你最喜欢正手击球，就为自己设立一个“投手丘”（即靠近底线的位置），然后大胆出击。如果你更喜欢正手网前击球，那就开始主动寻找上网的机会。不要等待对方的“邀请”（比如一个非常软弱的击球）。稍微主动一点，主动创造机会。

That personal pitcher’s mound for me is just behind the service T. It sets up my best weapon, the forehand approach shot to the ad court. I’m always looking to get that shot. I call it my equity shot because if I get it enough I’ll usually own the match. When I do get it I have great confidence in hitting it. Most players are the same. Know what it is that works for you and then actively try to get in position to use it.

>对我而言，那个个人的“投手丘”就在发球T点之后一点的位置。这里能摆出我最强的武器——正手直线截击球，打向对方的右侧底线。我总是想办法打出这个球。我称它为“我的保本球”，因为如果我能够经常打出它，通常就能掌控整场比赛。当我真的打出这个球时，我对自己击打它的信心非常强。大多数球员也都是这样。知道自己哪一种球最有效，然后积极地去创造机会使用它。

>[!note]- “equity shot”直译为“保本球”或“稳定球”，这里根据上下文意译为“保本球”，既保留原意，又符合中文表达习惯。

Another element that Ivan is a master at is stretching a lead. He may be the best there is at staying ahead when he gets ahead. And one of the reasons he’s effective at it is that he takes intelligent risks when he’s got the cushion of a lead. Not wild shots, but ones that are more forcing, more angled, more powerful. He likes to build on the momentum of getting ahead by upping the level and range of his game. He does it in a measured and calculated way. When he gets a lead the pressure he exerts is very noticeable, but he always operates within the boundaries of his game.

>伊万在另一个方面也堪称高手，那就是保持领先优势。他可能是在这方面最擅长的选手，一旦取得领先，他便能稳稳守住。其中一个重要原因在于，他在领先时会采取明智的冒险策略。他不会盲目冒险，而是选择更具压迫性、更具角度、更具威力的击球方式。他喜欢在取得领先后，通过提升自己的技术水平和击球范围，来延续这种势头。他总是有条不紊、深思熟虑地进行调整。一旦取得领先，他施加的压力非常明显，但他始终在自己的技术能力范围内运作。

When he’s ahead he starts going for his aces with more regularity and with more confidence, because he trusts his second serve. If he’s receiving serve he really tries to punish the ball, especially on his opponent’s second serve. Lendl waiting for a second serve is like inviting The Alien over for dinner. You know it’s not going to be fun. Ivan will totally destroy a weak second. It’s one of the reasons I’ve never beaten him. I’m forced to go with a weaker first serve to insure that I don’t let him see a second.

>当他处于领先时，他会更频繁、更有信心地发ACE球，因为他信任自己的二发。如果他接发球，他会特别努力地回击，尤其是对手的二发。伦德尔等待对手的二发，就像是邀请外星人来吃晚饭——你清楚这不会是件开心的事。伊万完全能摧毁一个弱的二发。这也是我从未赢过他的原因之一。我不得不使用较弱的一发，以确保他看不到我的二发。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“外星人”是比喻对手二发的威胁，意指其难以应对，故用“外星人”来强调其陌生与危险。

How does what he’s doing apply to you? When you get ahead increase the pressure on your opponent. Don’t be careless or swing wildly. Seize the opportunity to press your advantage and force your opponent to come up with more difficult shots.

>他这么做对你有什么启发呢？当你处于领先时，要加大对对手的压力。不要轻敌大意或盲目挥拍，要抓住机会扩大优势，迫使对手打出更困难的球。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“force your opponent to come up with more difficult shots”意为“迫使对手打出更困难的球”，在中文中可理解为“让对手在不利位置击球”，以保持原意的清晰性。

Finally, I want to stress Lendl’s great patience during a match. [[null|]]During the ’80s he maintained a mental discipline that was almost like Borg’s. Lendl never rushed into a point or through a shot. He was very methodical. Almost all recreational players are just the opposite. They (this means you ) get impatient. They attempt to hit the winner too soon. They want to make an approach shot more than it’s supposed to be (the approach shot sets up the winner—it isn’t supposed to be the winner).

>最后，我想强调伦德尔在比赛中所展现出的非凡耐心。[[null|]]在80年代，他保持了一种几乎与博格相媲美的心理纪律。伦德尔从不急于得分，也不仓促击球。他非常有条理、有计划。而几乎所有的业余球员则恰恰相反。你们（指的就是你们）总是不耐烦。你们过早地试图打出制胜球。你们过于追求打出进攻性击球，而实际上（进攻性击球只是为制胜球做铺垫，它本身并不是制胜球）。

I’ll watch two club players during a point and suddenly one of them will try and end it when they had no advantage, no opening, no reason to do so. They just got impatient. Lendl in the ’80s knew when to strike. He was patient. In fact, one of the reasons his game has suffered in the ’90s is that he isn’t as patient as he used to be. Maybe he just can’t wait to get home to his family, but he definitely doesn’t have the patience that he used to possess.

>我会观察两名业余选手在一分中的表现，突然其中一人会在自己毫无优势、毫无机会、毫无理由的情况下试图结束这一分。他们只是急躁了。上世纪80年代的莱德尔懂得何时出手，他很有耐心。事实上，他上世纪90年代以来球技下滑的一个重要原因，就是他不再像从前那样有耐心了。也许他只是迫不及待地想回家见家人，但他肯定已经失去了曾经拥有的那种耐心。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“can’t wait to get home”直译为“迫不及待回家”，但根据中文表达习惯，使用“想回家见家人”更自然流畅。

Learning From Lendl

>从伦德尔身上学习 /no_think

1\. Start the match at 65 percent of your power potential.

>1\. 从一开始就以你最大力量的65%来开局。

2\. Know where your own “personal pitcher’s mound” is and get to it.

>2\. 知道自己内心的“投手丘”在哪里，并前往那里。

3\. Stretch a lead by taking intelligent risks. Pressure your opponent when you’re ahead.

>3\. 通过采取明智的风险来扩大领先优势。当你处于领先位置时，要主动给对手施加压力。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此句强调在领先时也要保持警惕，主动出击，而不是放松防守，从而确保优势不被逆转。

4\. Be patient. Don’t force a shot that isn’t there.

>4\. 要有耐心。不要强行打出不存在的球。

>[!note]- 译注：原句中的“force a shot that isn’t there”意指不要强行制造不存在的击球机会，强调在比赛中应保持冷静，避免盲目进攻。

Ivan is great at maintaining an advantage, not so good at coming back when he’s behind. In fact, early in his career he would tank it occasionally when he got behind or didn’t want to play. Different players have different tendencies. I get cautious when I’m ahead and try to squeeze my opponent with steady tennis. Lendl likes to up the level of his game. It’s worth trying with your own tennis.

>伊万非常擅长保持领先优势，但一旦落后就很难翻盘。事实上，他职业生涯早期，一旦落后或者不想打了，有时就会彻底崩盘。不同的球员有不同的倾向。我领先时反而会变得谨慎，用稳定的网球压制对手。伦德尔则喜欢提升自己的比赛强度，这也是值得尝试的一种方式。

## 3 Boris Becker

>3 拜尔斯·贝克尔

Boris is an out-and-out superathlete, maybe the best one in pro tennis. You can just sense his eagerness to compete. He also has tremendous presence out on the court. By that I mean he plays big, and he plays big [[null|]]off of everything. He has heavy artillery, and with it he’s constantly putting pressure on you. It’s right here right now!

>博里斯绝对是一个彻头彻尾的超级运动员，也许是职业网球界最出色的选手之一。你几乎能感受到他对比赛的渴望。他在球场上也极具威慑力。我的意思是，他打球风格强势，无论面对什么情况都敢打敢拼。他拥有强大的武器，时刻对你施加压力。这正是现在！

The Becker serve is humongous. You can’t really get a sense of its weight watching him on TV. It just goes right through you. In addition, if his serve is on it allows him to take chances with other parts of his game because he knows he can come back with the Heater.

>贝克尔的发球威力巨大。你根本无法通过电视看他打球来真正感受它的分量，它只是直直地穿过你。此外，如果他的发球状态好，他就可以在其他技术环节上大胆冒险，因为他知道只要用上“ Heater”（他的发球），就一定能扭转局势。

>[!note]- “Heater”是贝克尔发球的昵称，意指其威力强大，可直接“加热”对手的防线。

Having said all that I haven’t even gotten to the strong part of his game: his self-confidence. At his best he’s so confident in his ability to come back or dictate play that he never doubts that he can win. He may get mad at himself, but he never thinks that he’s outgunned. He not only thinks he can beat you with his strengths, he believes he can beat you with his weaknesses. Total confidence. And Boris is similar to Lendl when it comes to stretching a lead. In fact, he will go further than Lendl and actually take more risks.

>我已经说了这么多，却还没谈到他打法中最强大的部分：他的自信心。在状态最好的时候，他对自己能够扭转局势或掌控比赛充满信心，从不怀疑自己能赢。他可能会对自己发火，但他绝不会觉得自己技不如人。他不仅相信自己能用自己的优势击败你，更相信自己即使凭借劣势也能取胜。这是一种彻底的自信。在拉长领先优势这一点上，波波维奇和伦德尔很相似。事实上，他甚至会比伦德尔更进一步，敢于采取更多冒险的策略。

Basic Becker

>基础贝克尔

1\. Believe in yourself. Think positive thoughts about your game and your ability to win.

>1\. 相信自己。对自己技术和赢球的能力抱有积极的信念。

2\. When you get a lead, go for it. Don’t be timid.

>2\. 得分领先时，要大胆进攻，不要怯场。

## 4 John McEnroe

>4 约翰·麦肯罗

When he was playing, John McEnroe’s hands had the precision, soft touch, and dexterity of a brain surgeon’s. He invented and started routinely using shots that most players had previously seen only in dreams. For example, in the early ’80s Mac would occasionally come to the net behind a weak approach shot and his opponent would absolutely crush the ball! Four or five times a match John would desperately lunge at the passing shot and not only get his racket on it, but he’d hit a soft, drop-shot winner. This is not taught currently by any tennis coach in the world. Try it. Believe me, if you succeed in doing it it’s an accident.

>约翰·麦肯罗打球时，他的双手精准如脑科医生，柔和而灵活。他发明并开始频繁使用那些以前大多数球员只能在梦中见过的击球方式。例如，在80年代初，麦克有时会在对手打出一个较弱的上网击球后，从网前快速冲过去，而对手则会把球狠狠砸向网前！每场比赛中，约翰都会拼命扑向对方的截击球，不仅成功接住，还能打出一个轻柔的压线球，直接得分。这种技术，目前世界上没有任何网球教练会教。试试看吧。相信我，如果你成功了，那纯粹是偶然。

But there are two tactical elements that John was known for that are worth considering. First, McEnroe played aggressively. He took the [[null|]]action right to his opponent. When he was playing well you felt the pressure before he even hit a ball because you knew he was going to start attacking. He wanted to see you make the passing shot against him. He wanted to see if you could make the passing shot against him. He got in close behind the net because he knew it was easier for you to choke at the baseline than for him to choke at the net. You knew that John was going to put his game right into your face.

>但约翰有两项战术特点值得一提。首先，麦肯罗打球非常积极主动。他总是把球直接打到对手的正面上方。当他状态好时，你甚至在他还没触球之前就能感受到压力，因为你知道他会立刻发起攻击。他希望你在他面前打出穿越网前的回球，他想看看你是否能在他面前打出这样的回球。他经常跑到网前，因为他知道，你站在底线位置更容易紧张，而他站在网前则更容易掌控局面。你清楚地知道，约翰一定会把他的战术直接摆在你面前。

Secondly, McEnroe was flexible. If you did start passing him or lobbing him successfully he adjusted. He could be an all-court player when it suited him. If you showed him the passing shot he would stay back and come in very selectively. His game (and mind) were very adaptable. He was a very smart and observant tennis player. He was always aware of the dynamics of the match and was looking for ways to exploit your weaknesses.

>其次，麦肯罗极具灵活性。如果你开始成功地用挑高球或大力平击球压制他，他也会相应调整。他可以根据需要变成全场型选手。如果你展示给他看挑高球的威力，他会后退站位，选择性地进入比赛。他的打法（以及思维方式）都非常灵活多变。他是一名非常聪明且善于观察的网球选手。他总是清楚比赛的局势，并且一直在寻找你弱点的突破口。

Mac’s Attack

>马可的进攻

1\. Probe. Aggressively search for your opponent’s weaknesses. Put pressure on them.

>1\. 探索。积极寻找对手的弱点，施加压力。

2\. Be flexible. If what you’re doing isn’t working, change.

>2\. 要有灵活性。如果你正在做的事情行不通，就换一种方式。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此句强调在比赛中保持思维和策略的灵活性，避免固守一种方法而无法适应变化。

One of the remarkable things about John’s game was that his great tennis skills were complemented by his intelligence on the court. He knew what he had and how to use it most effectively to exploit his opponent.

>约翰的球风之一令人印象深刻之处在于，他的卓越网球技术得到了他在球场上智慧的完美补充。他清楚自己拥有什么，并懂得如何最有效地运用这些优势来打击对手。

>[!note]- 译者注：
此处“exploit”翻译为“打击”而非直译“利用”，是为了更符合中文表达习惯，同时保留原意中的策略性攻击意味。

## 5 Stefan Edberg

>5 斯蒂芬·埃德伯格

Stefan’s tactical approach is the opposite of McEnroe’s. This is a good example of how different styles can be equally effective. McEnroe will test you here and test you there, trying to find a weakness and exploit it, coming in, staying back, constantly probing. Edberg’s approach is blunt: “I will serve and volley on every single point and attack the net constantly. If you want to beat me you’ll have to do it with me at the net.”

>斯蒂法诺的战术思路与麦肯罗完全相反。这是一个很好的例子，说明不同的风格同样可以取得成功。麦肯罗会在你这边试探，又在那边试探，试图找到你的弱点并加以利用，他常常上网，退守底线，不断施压。而埃德堡的打法则更为直接：“我将在每一个球点都发球上网，并持续不断地向网前进攻。如果你想击败我，就必须在我在网前的时候做到。”

He has polished his serve-volley game until there are no cracks [[null|]]or rough edges on it. His movement off the serve is just terrific. He jumps into the court on the serve so that he’s hitting his first volley from inside the service line most of the time. And he doesn’t miss that volley.

>他把发球抢网技术打磨得近乎完美，毫无破绽。他的发球后抢网移动也非常出色。他发球时就直接冲进网前，大多数情况下都能在发球线内完成第一拍网前击球，而且几乎从不失误。

Stefan will serve and volley twenty-two consecutive times. You can pass him cleanly twenty-two consecutive times. What’ll he do next? Number twenty-three will be a serve and volley. Whereas McEnroe will retreat to the baseline and look for something else to hurt you with, Edberg will force you to make the difficult shot one more time. And one more time. And one more time. You have to be very solid to pass someone like Edberg for the entire match.

>施特凡将连续发球上网22次。你可以干净利落地将他全部打回去。他接下来会怎么做呢？第23次依然是发球上网。而麦肯罗则会退到底线，寻找其他办法来伤害你。而埃德伯格则会让你再次面对那个困难的击球，一次又一次，一次又一次。你必须在整个比赛中非常稳健，才能将像埃德伯格这样的球员挡在外面。

He has no fear of anybody. Even if he’s getting passed regularly he knows he’s better off near the net. It takes a lot of pressure off him when it comes to deciding what to do next. Edberg’s fellow Swede (and my coauthor’s tennis hero) Bjorn Borg would stay on the baseline as relentlessly as Stefan attacks the net. He knew his game and he made you try to beat him when he was playing his strength.

>他无所畏惧，面对任何人都不惧。即使经常被对手过掉，他也清楚地知道，靠近网前对自己更有利。这让他在决定下一步行动时压力大大减轻。埃德伯格的同胞（也是我合著者的网球偶像）比约恩·伯格（Bjorn Borg）则会像施泰芬（Stefan）一样，持续不断地向网前施压。他深知自己的打法，而且在比赛中，他总能让你费尽心思才能击败他。

Stefan Edberg also has a great ability to cover a weakness. He has probably one of the weaker forehands of any number-one-ranked tennis player in the history of the game. He basically uses a backhand grip to hit a forehand groundstroke. He understands that and also has the ability to limit any damage it might cause.

>斯蒂法尼·埃德伯格也具备出色的弥补弱点的能力。他大概拥有历史上所有排名世界第一的网球选手中最弱的正手击球技术之一。他基本上是以反手握拍的方式击打正手底线球。他清楚这一点，也具备限制这种弱点可能造成负面影响的能力。

He offsets the damage in two ways. He takes his forehand out of play on his service games by coming to the net. The rest of the time when Stefan hits a forehand he doesn’t try to do more with it than he has to. He understands what it can do and doesn’t try to push more out of it. And he gets away with it. Remember the old saying, “Don’t fix it if it ain’t broke”? Well, his game “ain’t broke” and neither is Stefan. In 1990 he was ranked number one and earned $1,995,901. By 1993 he had won over $13,000,000. Maybe that’s why he hasn’t bothered to improve his forehand.

>他通过两种方式来弥补自己的不足。在发球局中，他会主动上网，把正手击球从对手的进攻范围中移出。其余时间，当施坦福打出正手时，他从不刻意去追求更多的进攻效果。他清楚自己的正手能做什么，也从不试图强行挖掘更多的潜力。他这样做的方式很奏效。还记得那句老话吗——“如果东西没坏，就别去修它”？他的打法“没坏”，施坦福也“没坏”。1990年，他排名世界第一，赚取了1300万美元。也许正因如此，他从未觉得有必要去改进自己的正手技术。

Also, like Borg, Stefan Edberg has total control of his emotions. Have you ever seen him get rattled or mad out on the court? On his way to winning the ’92 U.S. Open he was down a break in the fifth set both to Lendl in the quarters and to Chang in the semis. The look on his face [[null|]]was no different then from what it was at the start of the match. It told you nothing.
